         <td>31/23 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Belarus" title="Politics of Belarus">Politics of Belarus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg/220px-House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg/330px-House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg/440px-House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="663"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Government_House,_Minsk" title="Government House, Minsk">Government House, Minsk</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Belarus is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> republic, governed by a <a href="/wiki/President_of_Belarus" title="President of Belarus">president</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Belarus" title="National Assembly of Belarus">National Assembly</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Term_of_office" title="Term of office">term</a> for each presidency is five years. Under the 1994 constitution, the president could serve for only two terms as president, but a <a href="/wiki/2004_Belarusian_referendum" title="2004 Belarusian referendum">change in the constitution in 2004</a> eliminated term limits.<sup id="cite_ref-bbclukapro_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbclukapro-119">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Lukashenko" title="Alexander Lukashenko">Alexander Lukashenko</a> has been the president of Belarus since 1994. In 1996, Lukashenko called for a controversial vote to extend the presidential term from five to seven years, and as a result <a href="/wiki/2001_Belarusian_presidential_election" title="2001 Belarusian presidential election">the election</a> that was supposed to occur in 1999 was pushed back to 2001. The <a href="/wiki/1996_Belarusian_referendum" title="1996 Belarusian referendum">referendum on the extension</a> was denounced as a "fantastic" fake by the chief electoral officer, <a href="/wiki/Viktar_Hanchar" title="Viktar Hanchar">Viktar Hanchar</a>, who was removed from the office for official matters only during the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> The National Assembly is a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral parliament</a> comprising the 110-member <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Belarus" title="House of Representatives of Belarus">House of Representatives</a> (the lower house) and the 64-member <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Republic_of_Belarus" title="Council of the Republic of Belarus">Council of the Republic</a> (the upper house).<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Victory_square,_Minsk_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg/220px-Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg/330px-Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg/440px-Victory_square%2C_Minsk_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Victory_square,_Minsk_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Victory_Square,_Minsk" title="Victory Square, Minsk">Victory Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The House of Representatives has the power to appoint the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Belarusian_Prime_Ministers" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Belarusian Prime Ministers">prime minister</a>, make constitutional amendments, call for a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_Confidence" class="mw-redirect" title="Motion of Confidence">vote of confidence</a> on the prime minister, and make suggestions on foreign and domestic policy.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> The Council of the Republic has the power to select various government officials, conduct an impeachment trial of the president, and accept or reject the bills passed by the House of Representatives. Each chamber has the ability to veto any law passed by local officials if it is contrary to the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-conby_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conby-123">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government includes a Council of Ministers, headed by the prime minister and five deputy prime ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> The members of this council need not be members of the legislature and are appointed by the president. The judiciary comprises the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Belarus" title="Supreme Court of Belarus">Supreme Court</a> and specialized courts such as the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Belarus" title="Constitutional Court of Belarus">Constitutional Court</a>, which deals with specific issues related to constitutional and business law. The judges of national courts are appointed by the president and confirmed by the Council of the Republic. For criminal cases, the highest court of appeal is the Supreme Court. The Belarusian Constitution forbids the use of special extrajudicial courts.<sup id="cite_ref-conby_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conby-123">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/2012_Belarusian_parliamentary_election" title="2012 Belarusian parliamentary election">2012 parliamentary election</a>, 105 of the 110 members elected to the House of Representatives were not affiliated with any political party. The <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Belarus" title="Communist Party of Belarus">Communist Party of Belarus</a> won 3 seats, and the <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_Party_(Belarus)" title="Agrarian Party (Belarus)">Agrarian Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_of_Labour_and_Justice" title="Republican Party of Labour and Justice">Republican Party of Labour and Justice</a>, one each.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> Most non-partisans represent a wide scope of social organizations such as workers' collectives, public associations, and civil society organizations, similar to the composition of the Soviet legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg/220px-Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg/330px-Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg/440px-Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="685"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Solidarity_with_Belarus_concert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The former flag of Belarus, used in 1918 and then between 1991 and 1995, is widely used as a symbol of opposition to the government of Alexander Lukashenko.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Belarus has often been described as "Europe's last dictatorship" by some media outlets, politicians and authors due to its authoritarian government;<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters1_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1-128">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> Lukashenko has described himself as having an "<a href="/wiki/Authoritarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> ruling style".<sup id="cite_ref-bbclukapro_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbclukapro-119">[117]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> removed Belarus from its observer status since 1997 as a response for election irregularities in the November 1996 constitutional referendum and parliament by-elections.<sup id="cite_ref-CoE_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CoE-131">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> Re-admission of the country into the Council is dependent on the completion of benchmarks set by the Council, including the improvement of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Belarus" title="Human rights in Belarus">human rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a>, and democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Neither the pro-Lukashenko parties, such as the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Socialist_Sporting_Party" title="Belarusian Socialist Sporting Party">Belarusian Socialist Sporting Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_of_Labour_and_Justice" title="Republican Party of Labour and Justice">Republican Party of Labour and Justice</a>, nor the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Coalition_5_Plus" title="People's Coalition 5 Plus">People's Coalition 5 Plus</a> opposition parties, such as the <a href="/wiki/Partyja_BPF" class="mw-redirect" title="Partyja BPF">Belarusian People's Front</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Civil_Party_of_Belarus" class="mw-redirect" title="United Civil Party of Belarus">United Civil Party of Belarus</a>, won any seats in the <a href="/wiki/2004_Belarusian_parliamentary_election" title="2004 Belarusian parliamentary election">2004 elections</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE) ruled that the elections were unfair because opposition candidates were arbitrarily denied registration and the election process was designed to favor the ruling party.<sup id="cite_ref-OSCE_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSCE-134">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/2006_Belarusian_presidential_election" title="2006 Belarusian presidential election">2006 presidential election</a>, Lukashenko was opposed by <a href="/wiki/Alaksandar_Milinkievi%C4%8D" title="Alaksandar Milinkievič">Alaksandar Milinkievič</a>, who represented a coalition of opposition parties, and by <a href="/wiki/Alaksandar_Kazulin" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaksandar Kazulin">Alaksandar Kazulin</a> of the Social Democrats. Kazulin was detained and beaten by police during protests surrounding the <a href="/wiki/All_Belarusian_People%27s_Assembly" title="All Belarusian People's Assembly">All Belarusian People's Assembly</a>. Lukashenko won the election with 80% of the vote; the Russian Federation and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> deemed the vote open and fair<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> while the OSCE and other organizations called the election unfair.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the December completion of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Belarusian_presidential_election" title="2010 Belarusian presidential election">2010 presidential election</a>, Lukashenko was elected to a fourth straight term with nearly 80% of the vote in elections. The runner-up opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Sannikov" title="Andrei Sannikov">Andrei Sannikov</a> received less than 3% of the vote; independent observers criticized the election as fraudulent. When opposition protesters took to the streets in <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, many people, including most rival presidential candidates, were beaten and arrested by the state militia.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-137">[135]</a></sup> Many of the candidates, including Sannikov, were sentenced to prison or house arrest for terms which are mainly and typically over four years.<sup id="cite_ref-SannikovSentenced_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SannikovSentenced-138">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kyi_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kyi-139">[137]</a></sup> Six months later amid an unprecedented economic crisis, activists utilized social networking to initiate a fresh round of protests characterized by wordless hand-clapping.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/2020_Belarusian_presidential_election" title="2020 Belarusian presidential election">2020 presidential election</a> the official result was 80% for Lukashenko again. The election process and events afterwards have been criticized by representatives of many other countries. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights_and_corruption">Human rights and corruption</span></h3> 
      <p>Belarus's <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> rating is the lowest in Europe, the country is labelled as "not free" by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>, as "repressed" in the <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a>, and is rated as the worst country for <a href="/wiki/Press_freedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Press freedom">press freedom</a> in Europe in the <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">2013–2014 Press Freedom Index</a> published by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, which ranks Belarus 157th out of 180 nations.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> The Belarusian government is also criticized for human rights violations and its persecution of non-governmental organisations, independent journalists, national minorities, and opposition politicians.<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-20">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRW_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-90">[88]</a></sup> Lukashenko announced a new law in 2014 that will prohibit <a href="/wiki/Kolkhoz" title="Kolkhoz">kolkhoz</a> workers (around 9% of total work force) from leaving their jobs at will—a change of job and living location will require permission from governors. The law was compared with <a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">serfdom</a> by Lukashenko himself.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> Similar regulations were introduced for the forestry industry in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> Belarus is the only European country still using <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">capital punishment</a> having carried out executions in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The judicial system in Belarus lacks independence and is subject to political interference.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> Corrupt practices such as bribery often took place during tender processes, and <a href="/wiki/Whistleblower" title="Whistleblower">whistleblower</a> protection and national <a href="/wiki/Ombudsman" title="Ombudsman">ombudsman</a> are lacking in Belarus's anti-corruption system.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> However, there is a political will to fight against corruption in the government, and the government has made some progress in combating corruption, such as minimizing tax regulations in order to improve transparency in the tax office.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Belarus" title="Foreign relations of Belarus">Foreign relations of Belarus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Putin_with_Alexander_Lukashenko_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Putin_with_Alexander_Lukashenko_2015.jpg/220px-Putin_with_Alexander_Lukashenko_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Putin_with_Alexander_Lukashenko_2015.jpg/330px-Putin_with_Alexander_Lukashenko_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Putin_with_Alexander_Lukashenko_2015.jpg/440px-Putin_with_Alexander_Lukashenko_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Putin_with_Alexander_Lukashenko_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Lukashenko" title="Alexander Lukashenko">Alexander Lukashenko</a>, shaking hands with <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">Russian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Byelorussian SSR was one of the two Soviet republics that joined the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> along with the Ukrainian SSR as one of the original 51 members in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> Belarus and Russia have been close trading partners and diplomatic allies since the breakup of the Soviet Union. Belarus is dependent on Russia for imports of raw materials and for its export market.<sup id="cite_ref-stategov_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stategov-150">[148]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Russia_and_Belarus" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Russia and Belarus">union of Russia and Belarus</a>, a supranational confederation, was established in a 1996–99 series of treaties that called for monetary union, equal rights, single citizenship, and a common foreign and defense policy. However, the future of the union has been placed in doubt because of Belarus's repeated delays of monetary union, the lack of a referendum date for the draft constitution, and a <a href="/wiki/2007_Russia%E2%80%93Belarus_energy_dispute" title="2007 Russia–Belarus energy dispute">dispute over the petroleum trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stategov_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stategov-150">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> Belarus was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS).<sup id="cite_ref-cisstrained_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cisstrained-152">[150]</a></sup> Belarus has trade agreements with several <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states (despite other member states' travel ban on Lukashenko and top officials),<sup id="cite_ref-euban_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euban-153">[151]</a></sup> including neighboring Latvia, Lithuania, and Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-foreignrelations_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreignrelations-154">[152]</a></sup> Travel bans imposed by the European Union have been lifted in the past in order to allow Lukashenko to attend diplomatic meetings and also to engage his government and opposition groups in dialogue.<sup id="cite_ref-Belarus_president_visits_Vatican_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belarus_president_visits_Vatican-155">[153]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_(February_2015)_03.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg/220px-Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg/330px-Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg/440px-Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_%28February_2015%29_03.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="434"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Normandy_format_talks_in_Minsk_(February_2015)_03.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Leaders of Belarus, Russia, Germany, France, and Ukraine at the summit in <a href="/wiki/Minsk_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Minsk II">Minsk</a>, 11–12 February 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bilateral relations with the United States are strained; the United States had not had an ambassador in Minsk since 2007 and Belarus never had an ambassador in Washington since 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> Diplomatic relations remained tense, and in 2004, the United States passed the <a href="/wiki/Belarus_Democracy_Act_of_2004" title="Belarus Democracy Act of 2004">Belarus Democracy Act</a>, which authorized funding for anti-government Belarusian NGOs, and prohibited loans to the Belarusian government, except for humanitarian purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> Sino-Belarusian relations have improved,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> strengthened by the visit of President Lukashenko to China in October 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> Belarus also has strong ties with <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> considered a key partner in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> In addition to the CIS, Belarus is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Community" title="Eurasian Economic Community">Eurasian Economic Community</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">Collective Security Treaty Organisation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-foreignrelations_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreignrelations-154">[152]</a></sup> the international <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> since 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-byintorgs_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byintorgs-163">[161]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_on_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization on Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization on Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> (OSCE). As an OSCE member state, Belarus's international commitments are subject to monitoring under the mandate of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Helsinki_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Helsinki Commission">U.S. Helsinki Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> Belarus is included in the European Union's <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a> (ENP) which aims at bringing the EU and its neighbours closer in economic and geopolitical terms.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Belarus" title="Armed Forces of Belarus">Armed Forces of Belarus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="585"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_1047080_Work_of_%22Kamenyuki%22_frontier_post_on_Belarus_border_with_Poland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Soldiers patrol in the <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Białowieża Forest">Białowieża Forest</a> on the Belarusian border with Poland.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Major General <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Ravkov" title="Andrei Ravkov">Andrei Ravkov</a> heads the Ministry of Defence,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup> and Alexander Lukashenko (as president) serves as Commander-in-Chief.<sup id="cite_ref-conby_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conby-123">[121]</a></sup> The armed forces were formed in 1992 using parts of the former <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Armed_Forces" title="Soviet Armed Forces">Soviet Armed Forces</a> on the new republic's territory. The transformation of the ex-Soviet forces into the Armed Forces of Belarus, which was completed in 1997, reduced the number of its soldiers by 30,000 and restructured its leadership and military formations.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most of Belarus's service members are <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscripts</a>, who serve for 12 months if they have higher education or 18 months if they do not.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> Demographic decreases in the Belarusians of conscription age have increased the importance of contract soldiers, who numbered 12,000 in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-conscripts_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conscripts-169">[167]</a></sup> In 2005, about 1.4% of Belarus's gross domestic product was devoted to military expenditure.<sup id="cite_ref-ciabymil_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciabymil-170">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Belarus has not expressed a desire to join <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> but has participated in the Individual Partnership Program since 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> and Belarus provides refueling and airspace support for the <a href="/wiki/ISAF" class="mw-redirect" title="ISAF">ISAF</a> mission in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> Belarus first began to cooperate with NATO upon signing documents to participate in their Partnership for Peace Program in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> However, Belarus cannot join NATO because it is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">Collective Security Treaty Organisation</a>. Tensions between NATO and Belarus peaked after the March 2006 presidential election in Belarus.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Belarus" title="Regions of Belarus">Regions of Belarus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Belarus" title="Districts of Belarus">Districts of Belarus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Belarus,_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Belarus%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png/220px-Belarus%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Belarus%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png/330px-Belarus%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Belarus%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png/440px-Belarus%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png 2x" data-file-width="6784" data-file-height="6058"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Belarus,_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Administrative divisions of Belarus
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Belarus is divided into six <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">regions</a> (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">вобласць</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">о́бласть</span>), which are named after the cities that serve as their administrative centers: <a href="/wiki/Brest,_Belarus" title="Brest, Belarus">Brest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gomel" title="Gomel">Gomel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grodno" title="Grodno">Grodno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mogilev" title="Mogilev">Mogilev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vitebsk" title="Vitebsk">Vitebsk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-s1_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-175">[173]</a></sup> Each region has a provincial legislative authority, called a region council (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">абласны Савет Дэпутатаў</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">областно́й Сове́т Депутатов</span>), which is elected by its residents, and a provincial executive authority called a region administration (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">абласны выканаўчы камітэт</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">областно́й исполнительный комите́т</span>), whose chairman is appointed by the president.<sup id="cite_ref-s5_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s5-176">[174]</a></sup> Regions are further subdivided into <i><a href="/wiki/Raion" title="Raion">raions</a></i>, commonly translated as <i>districts</i> (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">раён</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">район</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-s1_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-175">[173]</a></sup> Each <i>raion</i> has its own legislative authority, or <i>raion</i> council, (<a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>: <span lang="be">раённы Савет Дэпутатаў</span>, Russian: <span lang="ru">районный Сове́т Депутатов</span>) elected by its residents, and an executive authority or <i>raion</i> administration appointed by higher executive powers. The six regions are divided into 118 <i>raions</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-key_facts_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-key_facts-107">[105]</a></sup> The city of Minsk is split into nine districts and enjoys special status as the nation's capital.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup> It is run by an executive committee and has been granted a charter of self-rule.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Belarus" title="Economy of Belarus">Economy of Belarus</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Belarusian_regions_by_GRP" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Belarusian regions by GRP">List of Belarusian regions by GRP</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg/310px-Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg" decoding="async" width="310" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg/465px-Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg/620px-Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="924" data-file-height="719"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Belarus.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A graphical depiction of Belarus's product exports in 28&nbsp;colour-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2014 the share of manufacturing in GDP was 37%, more than two thirds of this amount falls on manufacturing industries. The number of people employed in industry is 32.7% of the working population. The growth rate is much lower than for the economy as a whole—about 1.9% in 2014. At the time of the dissolution of the Soviet Union in 1991, Belarus was one of the world's most industrially developed states by percentage of GDP as well as the richest CIS member-state.<sup id="cite_ref-wb97_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb97-179">[177]</a></sup> In 2015, 39.3% of Belarusians were employed by state-controlled companies, 57.2% were employed by private companies (in which the government has a 21.1% stake) and 3.5% were employed by foreign companies.<sup id="cite_ref-econstats_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econstats-180">[178]</a></sup> The country relies on Russia for various imports, including petroleum.<sup id="cite_ref-natotrade_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natotrade-181">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> Important agricultural products include potatoes and cattle byproducts, including meat.<sup id="cite_ref-ciaecon_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciaecon-183">[181]</a></sup> In 1994, Belarus's main exports included heavy machinery (especially <a href="/wiki/Belarus_(tractor)" title="Belarus (tractor)">tractors</a>), agricultural products, and energy products.<sup id="cite_ref-byexports_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byexports-184">[182]</a></sup> Economically, Belarus involved itself in the CIS, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Community" title="Eurasian Economic Community">Eurasian Economic Community</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Union_State" title="Union State">Union with Russia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In the 1990s, however, industrial production plunged due to decreases in imports, investment, and demand for Belarusian products from its trading partners.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> GDP only began to rise in 1996;<sup id="cite_ref-bybriefwb06_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bybriefwb06-186">[184]</a></sup> the country was the fastest-recovering former Soviet republic in the terms of its economy.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> In 2006, GDP amounted to <span class="nowrap">US$83.1 billion</span> in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP) dollars (estimate), or about $8,100 per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-ciaecon_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciaecon-183">[181]</a></sup> In 2005, GDP increased by 9.9%; the inflation rate averaged 9.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-ciaecon_183-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciaecon-183">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the disintegration of the Soviet Union, under Lukashenko's leadership, Belarus has maintained government control over key industries and eschewed the large-scale privatizations seen in other former Soviet republics.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006, Belarus's largest trading partner was Russia, accounting for nearly half of total trade, with the European Union the next largest trading partner, with nearly a third of foreign trade.<sup id="cite_ref-tradestats_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tradestats-188">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eutrade_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eutrade-189">[187]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belarus&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 38% of Belarusian exported goods go to Russia and 56% of imported goods come from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-econstats_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econstats-180">[178]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg/310px-Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="310" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg/465px-Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg/620px-Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1383" data-file-height="877"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Belarus_-_Annual_GDP_and_CPI_rates_2001-2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Belarusian annual GDP and CPI rates 2001–2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Due to its failure to protect labor rights, including passing laws forbidding unemployment or working outside of state-controlled sectors,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> Belarus lost its EU <a href="/wiki/Generalized_System_of_Preferences" title="Generalized System of Preferences">Generalized System of Preferences</a> status on <span class="nowrap">21 June</span> 2007, which raised tariff rates to their prior <a href="/wiki/Most_favored_nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Most favored nation">most favored nation</a> levels.<sup id="cite_ref-eutrade_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eutrade-189">[187]</a></sup> Belarus applied to become a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The labor force consists of more than four million people, among whom women hold slightly more jobs than men.<sup id="cite_ref-econstats_180-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econstats-180">[178]</a></sup> In 2005, nearly a quarter of the population was employed by industrial factories. Employment is also high in agriculture, manufacturing sales, trading goods, and education. The unemployment rate, according to government statistics, was 1.5% in 2005. There were 679,000 unemployed Belarusians, two-thirds of whom were women. The unemployment rate has been in decline since 2003, and the overall rate of employment is the highest since statistics were first compiled in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-econstats_180-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econstats-180">[178]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The currency of Belarus is the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_ruble" title="Belarusian ruble">Belarusian ruble</a>. The currency was introduced in May 1992 to replace the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_ruble" title="Soviet ruble">Soviet ruble</a> and it has undergone <a href="/wiki/Redenomination" title="Redenomination">redenomination</a> twice since then. The first coins of the Republic of Belarus were issued on 27 December 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup> The ruble was reintroduced with new values in 2000 and has been in use ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> As part of the <a href="/wiki/Union_State" title="Union State">Union of Russia and Belarus</a>, both states have discussed using a single currency along the same lines as the Euro. This led to a proposal that the Belarusian ruble be discontinued in favor of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">Russian ruble</a> (RUB), starting as early as <span class="nowrap">1 January</span> 2008. The <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_the_Republic_of_Belarus" title="National Bank of the Republic of Belarus">National Bank of Belarus</a> abandoned pegging the Belarusian ruble to the Russian ruble in August 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A new currency, the <a href="/wiki/New_Belarusian_ruble" class="mw-redirect" title="New Belarusian ruble">new Belarusian ruble</a> (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">ISO 4217</a> code: BYN)<sup id="cite_ref-currency-iso.org_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-currency-iso.org-195">[193]</a></sup> was introduced in July 2016, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_ruble" title="Belarusian ruble">Belarusian ruble</a> in a rate of 1:10,000 (10,000 old rubles = 1 new ruble). From 1 July until 31 December 2016, the old and new currencies were in parallel circulation and series 2000 notes and coins can be exchanged for series 2009 from 1 January 2017 to 31 December 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-currency-iso.org_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-currency-iso.org-195">[193]</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Redenomination" title="Redenomination">redenomination</a> can be considered an effort to fight the high inflation rate.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The banking system of Belarus consists of two levels: Central Bank (National Bank of the Republic of Belarus) and 25 commercial banks.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup> On 23 May 2011, the Belarusian ruble depreciated 56% against the United States dollar. The depreciation was even steeper on the black market and financial collapse seemed imminent as citizens rushed to exchange their rubles for dollars, euros, durable goods, and canned goods.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> On 1 June 2011, Belarus requested an economic rescue package from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Belarus" title="Demographics of Belarus">Demographics of Belarus</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the census of 2019, the population was 9.41 million,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-202">[200]</a></sup> and ethnic <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a> constitute 84.9% of Belarus's total population.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_202-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-202">[200]</a></sup> Belarus has a proper minority of other <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> from its neighbouring countries; as the next largest ethnic groups are: <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> (7.5%), <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> (3.1%), and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> (1.7%).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_202-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-202">[200]</a></sup> Belarus has a population density of about 50 people per square kilometer (127 per sq&nbsp;mi); 70% of its total population is concentrated in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, the nation's capital and largest city, was home to 1,937,900 residents in 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belarus&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gomel" title="Gomel">Gomel</a>, with a population of 481,000, is the second-largest city and serves as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Homiel_Voblast" class="mw-redirect" title="Homiel Voblast">Homiel Voblast</a>. Other large cities are <a href="/wiki/Mogilev" title="Mogilev">Mogilev</a> (365,100), <a href="/wiki/Vitebsk" title="Vitebsk">Vitebsk</a> (342,400), <a href="/wiki/Hrodna" class="mw-redirect" title="Hrodna">Hrodna</a> (314,800) and <a href="/wiki/Brest,_Belarus" title="Brest, Belarus">Brest</a> (298,300).<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[203]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Like many other Eastern European countries, Belarus has a negative population growth rate and a negative natural growth rate. In 2007, Belarus's population declined by 0.41% and its <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">fertility rate</a> was 1.22,<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-206">[204]</a></sup> well <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility" title="Sub-replacement fertility">below the replacement rate</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Net_migration_rate" title="Net migration rate">net migration rate</a> is +0.38 per 1,000, indicating that Belarus experiences slightly more immigration than emigration. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belarus&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 69.9% of Belarus's population is aged 14 to 64; 15.5% is under 14, and 14.6% is 65 or older. Its population is also aging; the median age of 30–34 is estimated to rise to between 60 and 64 in 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[205]</a></sup> There are about 0.87 males per female in Belarus.<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-206">[204]</a></sup> The average life expectancy is 72.15 (66.53 years for men and 78.1 years for women).<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_206-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-206">[204]</a></sup> Over 99% of Belarusians aged 15 and older are <a href="/wiki/Literate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literate">literate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-demographics_206-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-206">[204]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p> 
      <table class="navbox"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="10" class="navbox-title">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion_and_languages">Religion and languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Belarus" title="Religion in Belarus">Religion in Belarus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Belarus" title="Languages of Belarus">Languages of Belarus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/220px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg 2x" data-file-width="714" data-file-height="534"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%BA._%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%84%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Saint_Sophia_Cathedral_in_Polotsk" title="Saint Sophia Cathedral in Polotsk">Saint Sophia Cathedral in Polotsk</a> is one of the oldest churches in Belarus. Its current style is an ideal example of <a href="/wiki/Baroque_in_Poland" title="Baroque in Poland">baroque architecture</a> in the former <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the census of November 2011, 58.9% of all Belarusians adhered to some kind of religion; out of those, <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Orthodox_Church" title="Belarusian Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodoxy</a> (Belarusian Exarchate of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>) made up about 82%.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa-208">[206]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Belarus" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Belarus">Roman Catholicism</a> is practiced mostly in the western regions, and there are also different denominations of Protestantism.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[207]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup> Minorities also practice <a href="/wiki/Greek_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Catholicism">Greek Catholicism</a>, Judaism, Islam and Neopaganism. Overall, 48.3% of the population is Orthodox Christian, 41.1% is not religious, 7.1% is Catholic and 3.3% follows other religions.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa-208">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Belarus's Catholic minority is concentrated in the western part of the country, especially around <a href="/wiki/Hrodna" class="mw-redirect" title="Hrodna">Hrodna</a>, is made up of a mixture of Belarusians and the country's <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithuanian people">Lithuanian</a> minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-Belarus_–_Religion_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belarus_–_Religion-211">[209]</a></sup> President Lukashenko has stated that Orthodox and Catholic believers are the "two main confessions in our country".<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[210]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Belarus was once a major center of European Jews, with 10% of the population being <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Belarus" title="History of the Jews in Belarus">Jewish</a>. But since the mid-20th century, the number of Jews has been reduced by the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>, deportation, and emigration, so that today it is a very small minority of less than one percent.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[211]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lipka_Tatars" title="Lipka Tatars">Lipka Tatars</a>, numbering over 15,000, are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Belarus" title="Islam in Belarus">Muslims</a>. According to Article 16 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Belarus" title="Constitution of Belarus">Constitution</a>, Belarus has no official religion. While the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of worship</a> is granted in the same article, religious organizations deemed harmful to the government or social order can be prohibited.<sup id="cite_ref-s1_175-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-175">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Belarus's two official languages are Russian and <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup> Russian is the most common language used at home, used by 70% of the population, while Belarusian, the official first language, is spoken at home by 23%.<sup id="cite_ref-2009-census-languages_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009-census-languages-215">[213]</a></sup> Minorities also speak <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Yiddish" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Yiddish">Eastern Yiddish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[214]</a></sup> Belarusian, although not as widely used as Russian, is the mother tongue of 53.2% of the population, whereas Russian is the mother tongue of only 41.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-2009-census-languages_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009-census-languages-215">[213]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Belarus" title="Culture of Belarus">Culture of Belarus</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_literature">Arts and literature</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D1%8B%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8D%D0%BC%D1%96%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%92%D1%8F%D0%BB%D1%96%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%82%D1%8D%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%8D%D1%80%D1%8B_%D1%96_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%D0%B3._%D0%9C%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA_2.jpg/330px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D1%8B%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8D%D0%BC%D1%96%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%92%D1%8F%D0%BB%D1%96%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%82%D1%8D%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%8D%D1%80%D1%8B_%D1%96_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%D0%B3._%D0%9C%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D1%8B%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8D%D0%BC%D1%96%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%92%D1%8F%D0%BB%D1%96%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%82%D1%8D%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%8D%D1%80%D1%8B_%D1%96_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%D0%B3._%D0%9C%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA_2.jpg/440px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D1%8B%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8D%D0%BC%D1%96%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%92%D1%8F%D0%BB%D1%96%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%82%D1%8D%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%8D%D1%80%D1%8B_%D1%96_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%D0%B3._%D0%9C%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3386" data-file-height="2712"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D1%8B%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8D%D0%BC%D1%96%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%92%D1%8F%D0%BB%D1%96%D0%BA%D1%96_%D1%82%D1%8D%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%8D%D1%80%D1%8B_%D1%96_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%83_%D0%B3._%D0%9C%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Opera_and_Ballet_of_Belarus" title="National Opera and Ballet of Belarus">Opera and Ballet Theater</a> in Minsk
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Belarusian government sponsors annual cultural festivals such as the <a href="/wiki/Slavianski_Bazaar_in_Vitebsk" title="Slavianski Bazaar in Vitebsk">Slavianski Bazaar in Vitebsk</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[215]</a></sup> which showcases Belarusian performers, artists, writers, musicians, and actors. Several state holidays, such as <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Independence_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by Independence Day">Independence Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victory_Day_(9_May)" title="Victory Day (9 May)">Victory Day</a>, draw big crowds and often include displays such as fireworks and military parades, especially in Vitebsk and Minsk.<sup id="cite_ref-festivals_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-festivals-218">[216]</a></sup> The government's Ministry of Culture finances events promoting Belarusian arts and culture both inside and outside the country. </p>
      <p>Belarusian literature<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[217]</a></sup> began with 11th- to 13th-century religious scripture, such as the 12th-century poetry of <a href="/wiki/Cyril_of_Turaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyril of Turaw">Cyril of Turaw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bypoem_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bypoem-220">[218]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By the 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Polotsk" title="Polotsk">Polotsk</a> resident <a href="/wiki/Francysk_Skaryna" title="Francysk Skaryna">Francysk Skaryna</a> translated the Bible into Belarusian. It was published in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vilnius" title="Vilnius">Vilnius</a> sometime between 1517 and 1525, making it the first book printed in Belarus or anywhere in Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-byeb_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byeb-221">[219]</a></sup> The modern era of Belarusian literature began in the late 19th century; one prominent writer was <a href="/wiki/Yanka_Kupala" title="Yanka Kupala">Yanka Kupala</a>. Many Belarusian writers of the time, such as <a href="/wiki/U%C5%82adzimir_%C5%BDy%C5%82ka" title="Uładzimir Žyłka">Uładzimir Žyłka</a>, Kazimir Svayak, <a href="/wiki/Yakub_Kolas" title="Yakub Kolas">Yakub Kolas</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%B9mitrok_Biadula" title="Źmitrok Biadula">Źmitrok Biadula</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maksim_Haretski" title="Maksim Haretski">Maksim Haretski</a>, wrote for <i><a href="/wiki/Nasha_Niva" title="Nasha Niva">Nasha Niva</a></i>, a Belarusian-language paper published that was previously published in Vilnius but now is published in Minsk.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[220]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After Belarus was incorporated into the Soviet Union, the Soviet government took control of the Republic's cultural affairs. At first, a policy of "Belarusianization" was followed in the newly formed Byelorussian SSR. This policy was reversed in the 1930s, and the majority of prominent Belarusian intellectuals and nationalist advocates were either exiled or killed in Stalinist purges.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[221]</a></sup> The free development of literature occurred only in Polish-held territory until Soviet occupation in 1939. Several poets and authors went into exile after the Nazi occupation of Belarus and would not return until the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-byeb_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byeb-221">[219]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg/170px-Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg/255px-Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg/340px-Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="681" data-file-height="1126"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wincenty_Dunin-Marcinkiewicz_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Poet and librettist <a href="/wiki/Vintsent_Dunin-Martsinkyevich" title="Vintsent Dunin-Martsinkyevich">Vintsent Dunin-Martsinkyevich</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The last major revival of Belarusian literature occurred in the 1960s with novels published by <a href="/wiki/Vasil_Byka%C5%AD" title="Vasil Bykaŭ">Vasil Bykaŭ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uladzimir_Karatkievich" title="Uladzimir Karatkievich">Uladzimir Karatkievich</a>. An influential author who devoted his work to awakening the awareness of the catastrophes the country has suffered, was <a href="/wiki/Ales_Adamovich" title="Ales Adamovich">Ales Adamovich</a>. He was named by <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Alexievich" title="Svetlana Alexievich">Svetlana Alexievich</a>, the Belarusian winner of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> 2015, as "her main teacher, who helped her to find a path of her own".<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[222]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Belarus" title="Music of Belarus">Music in Belarus</a> largely comprises a rich tradition of folk and religious music. The country's folk music traditions can be traced back to the times of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>. In the 19th century, Polish composer <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Moniuszko" title="Stanisław Moniuszko">Stanisław Moniuszko</a> composed operas and chamber music pieces while living in Minsk. During his stay, he worked with Belarusian poet <a href="/wiki/Vintsent_Dunin-Martsinkyevich" title="Vintsent Dunin-Martsinkyevich">Vintsent Dunin-Martsinkyevich</a> and created the opera <i>Sialanka</i> (<i>Peasant Woman</i>). At the end of the 19th century, major Belarusian cities formed their own opera and ballet companies. The ballet <i><a href="/wiki/Nightingale_(ballet)" title="Nightingale (ballet)">Nightingale</a></i> by M. Kroshner was composed during the Soviet era and became the first Belarusian ballet showcased at the National Academic Vialiki Ballet Theatre in Minsk.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[223]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, music focused on the hardships of the Belarusian people or on those who took up arms in defense of the homeland. During this period, <a href="/wiki/Anatoly_Bogatyrev" title="Anatoly Bogatyrev">Anatoly Bogatyrev</a>, creator of the opera <i>In Polesye Virgin Forest</i>, served as the "tutor" of Belarusian composers.<sup id="cite_ref-clasmus_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clasmus-226">[224]</a></sup> The National Academic Theatre of Ballet in Minsk was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Prix_Benois_de_la_Danse" title="Prix Benois de la Danse">Benois de la Dance Prize</a> in 1996 as the top ballet company in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-clasmus_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clasmus-226">[224]</a></sup> Rock music has become increasingly popular in recent years, though the Belarusian government has attempted to limit the amount of foreign music aired on the radio in favor of traditional Belarusian music. Since 2004, Belarus has been sending artists to the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[226]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Marc_Chagall" title="Marc Chagall">Marc Chagall</a> was born in Liozna (near <a href="/wiki/Vitebsk" title="Vitebsk">Vitebsk</a>) in 1887. He spent the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> years in Soviet Belarus, becoming one of the country's most distinguished artists and a member of the modernist <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> and was a founder of the Vitebsk Arts College.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[228]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dress">Dress</span></h3> 
      <p>The traditional Belarusian dress originates from the <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a> period. Due to the cool climate, clothes were designed to preserve body heat and were usually made from <a href="/wiki/Flax" title="Flax">flax</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>. They were decorated with ornate patterns influenced by the neighboring cultures: Poles, Lithuanians, Latvians, Russians, and other European nations. Each region of Belarus has developed specific design patterns.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[229]</a></sup> One ornamental pattern common in early dresses currently decorates the hoist of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Belarus" title="Flag of Belarus">Belarusian national flag</a>, adopted in a <a href="/wiki/1995_Belarusian_referendum" title="1995 Belarusian referendum">disputed referendum</a> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[230]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Potato_pancakes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Potato_pancakes.jpg/220px-Potato_pancakes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Potato_pancakes.jpg/330px-Potato_pancakes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Potato_pancakes.jpg/440px-Potato_pancakes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Potato_pancakes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Potato_pancake" title="Potato pancake">Draniki</a>, the national dish
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Belarusian_cuisine" title="Belarusian cuisine">Belarusian cuisine</a> consists mainly of vegetables, meat (particularly pork), and bread. Foods are usually either slowly cooked or <a href="/wiki/Stewed" class="mw-redirect" title="Stewed">stewed</a>. Typically, Belarusians eat a light breakfast and two hearty meals later in the day. <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">Wheat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rye" title="Rye">rye</a> breads are consumed in Belarus, but rye is more plentiful because conditions are too harsh for growing wheat. To show hospitality, a host traditionally presents an offering of <a href="/wiki/Bread_and_salt" title="Bread and salt">bread and salt</a> when greeting a guest or visitor.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[231]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>
